2:19:859:0:14:72:163:700:12:Times:12:Times:?:Taxes and Turnout
2:20:876:14:14:72:356:686:12:Times:12:g_d0_f1:?:Felix Bierbrauer, Aleh Tsyvinski, and Nicolas D. Werquin 
2:21:932:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:?:NBER Working Paper No. 24123
2:22:960:14:14:72:148:658:12:Times:12:g_d0_f3:?:December 2017
2:23:973:14:28:71:182:644:12:Times:12:Times:?:JEL No. D72,D82,H21
2:24:992:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:?:ABSTRACT
2:25:1000:28:14:72:545:588:12:Times:12:g_d0_f2:?:We develop a model of political competition with endogenous turnout and endogenous platforms. 
2:26:1093:14:14:72:546:574:12:Times:12:Times:?:Parties  face  a  trade-off  between  maximizing  their  base  and  getting  their  supporters  out  to  vote. 
2:27:1204:14:14:72:546:560:12:Times:12:Times:?:We study the implications of this framework for non-linear income taxation. In equilibrium, both 
2:28:1300:14:14:72:546:546:12:Times:12:Times:?:parties propose  the  same  tax  policy.  This  equilibrium  policy  is  a  weighted  combination  of  two 
2:29:1406:14:14:72:546:532:12:Times:12:Times:?:terms, one reflecting the parties’ payoff from mobilizing their own supporters, one reflecting the 
2:30:1504:14:14:72:546:518:12:Times:12:Times:?:payoff  from demobilizing  the  supporters  of  the  other  party.  The  key  determinant  of  the 
2:31:1602:14:14:71:545:504:12:Times:12:Times:?:equilibrium policy is the distribution of the voters’ party attachments rather than their propensity 
2:32:1702:14:14:72:545:490:12:Times:12:Times:?:to  swing  vote.  Our  analysis also  provides  a  novel  explanation  for  why  even  left-leaning  parties 
2:33:1810:14:42:72:260:476:12:Times:12:Times:?:may not propose high taxes on the rich.
2:34:1848:42:14:72:151:434:12:Times:12:Times:?:Felix Bierbrauer
2:35:1864:14:14:72:286:420:12:Times:12:Times:?:CMR - Center for Macroeconomic Research
2:36:1903:14:14:72:179:406:12:Times:12:Times:?:University of Cologne
2:37:1924:14:14:72:172:392:12:Times:12:Times:?:Albert-Magnus Platz
2:38:1943:14:14:72:146:378:12:Times:12:Times:?:50923 Cologne
2:39:1956:14:14:72:117:364:12:Times:12:Times:?:Germany
2:40:1963:14:28:72:218:350:12:Times:12:Times:?:bierbrauer@wiso.uni-koeln.de
2:41:1991:28:14:72:146:322:12:Times:12:Times:?:Aleh Tsyvinski
2:42:2005:14:14:72:198:308:12:Times:12:Times:?:Department of Economics
2:43:2028:14:14:72:148:294:12:Times:12:Times:?:Yale University
2:44:2043:14:14:72:131:280:12:Times:12:Times:?:Box 208268

2:46:2078:14:14:72:124:252:12:Times:12:Times:?:and NBER
2:47:2086:14:0:72:175:238:12:Times:12:Times:?:a.tsyvinski@yale.edu
2:48:2106:0:14:306:402:434:12:Times:12:Times:?:Nicolas D. Werquin
2:49:2124:14:14:306:456:420:12:Times:12:Times:?:Toulouse School of Economics
2:50:2152:14:14:306:399:406:12:Times:12:Times:?:21 allee de Brienne
2:51:2171:14:14:306:387:392:12:Times:12:Times:?:31000 Toulouse

3:53:2204:0:30:90:192:690:17:g_d0_f4:17:g_d0_f4:C:Introduction
3:54:2216:30:18:90:522:660:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:To win in an election, parties need to get their supporters out to vote. This paper
3:55:2299:18:17:90:522:642:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:develops a model of political competition with two political parties that seek to max-
3:56:2385:17:18:90:522:625:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:imize the probability of winning an election. The electorate includes rule-utilitarian
3:57:2471:18:17:90:522:607:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:voters who participate in an election only if the benefits of a victory of their preferred
3:58:2561:17:18:90:522:590:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:party outweigh the costs of voting. That is, participation is endogenous. Parties pro-
3:59:2647:18:18:90:522:572:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:pose policies taking into account these implications for turnout. That is, policies are
3:60:2734:18:17:90:522:554:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:endogenous. We show that parties face a trade-off between maximizing their base,
3:61:2814:17:18:90:522:537:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:defined as the mass of citizens who are better off if the party wins, and getting their
3:62:2901:18:18:90:522:519:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:supporters out to vote. This in turn translates into the central determinant of the
3:63:2984:18:17:90:522:501:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:choice of policies, namely, a trade-off between mobilizing one’s own supporters and
3:64:3067:17:18:90:274:484:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:demobilizing those of the adversary.
3:65:3103:18:17:107:522:466:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Our formal analysis combines the probabilistic voting model due toCoughlin and
3:66:3181:17:18:89:521:449:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Nitzan(1981) andLindbeck and Weibull(1987) with the models of participation
3:67:3256:18:18:89:521:431:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:in elections due toHarsanyi(1980),Coate and Conlin(2004) andFeddersen and
3:68:3329:18:17:89:521:413:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Sandroni(2006). In probabilistic voting models it is assumed that parties maximize
3:69:3411:17:18:89:521:396:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:their vote shares and voters trade off idiosyncratic party preferences with the utility
3:70:3498:18:18:89:521:378:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:they derive from the platforms that the competing parties propose.1Appropriate
3:71:3576:18:17:89:521:360:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:assumptions on the distribution of party preferences then ensure that equilibrium
3:72:3657:17:18:89:521:343:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:policies are well-defined and the focus is on the characterization of the policies that
3:73:3744:18:17:89:521:325:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:emerge in a probabilistic voting equilibrium. It is, however, assumed that everyone
3:74:3827:17:18:89:521:308:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:who is eligible to vote participates in the election. This assumption is relaxed by
3:75:3910:18:18:89:521:290:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the literature that treats turnout as an endogenous political equilibrium outcome.
3:76:3992:18:17:89:521:272:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:We follow the literature that models participation in an election as the outcome of
3:77:4075:17:18:89:521:255:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:a rule-utilitarian calculation.  The supporters, say, of party 1 formulate a rule for
3:78:4160:18:18:89:521:237:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:participating in an election that trades off what is at stake for the supporters of party
3:79:4249:18:17:89:522:219:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:1 against their costs of voting. As has been shown byCoate and Conlin(2004) and
3:80:4328:17:18:89:521:202:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Feddersen and Sandroni(2006), this approach yields comparative statics properties
3:81:4409:18:17:89:521:184:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of turnout that are consistent with stylized facts about participation in elections, e.g.,
3:82:4499:17:18:89:521:167:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:participation is larger the closer is the race between the two alternatives, or the more
3:83:4587:18:18:89:521:149:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:polarized preferences are. The literature on endogenous turnout views the alternatives
3:84:4673:18:26:89:521:131:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:in an election as exogenously given, however. Choices are between a competitor and
3:85:4755:26:15:106:522:105:7:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f8:F:1The probabilistic voting model is a special case of what has been coined a random participation
3:86:4851:15:0:89:241:90:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:model by Rochet and Stole(2002).
4:87:4884:0:18:90:522:690:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:an incumbent, or between a reform and a status quo so that there is no analysis
4:88:4963:18:18:90:522:672:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of a party’s problem to refine the alternatives that are proposed so as to achieve a
4:89:5047:18:17:90:522:654:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:higher turnout of its supporters and thereby a higher probability of winning. With
4:90:5129:17:18:90:522:637:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:our approach, both the platform choices of parties and the turnout decisions of voters
4:91:5215:18:18:90:222:619:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:are equilibrium outcomes.
4:92:5240:18:17:107:521:601:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:It is a frequent observation that individuals with high incomes are more likely
4:93:5319:17:18:90:522:584:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:to participate in elections than individuals with low incomes.  We therefore study
4:94:5401:18:17:90:522:566:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the implications of our approach for a policy domain that allows for a differential
4:95:5484:17:18:90:522:549:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:treatment of individuals with different incomes. A natural policy space is therefore
4:96:5568:18:18:90:522:531:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:to consider non-linear income tax schedules, so that parties can propose tax schedules
4:97:5654:18:17:90:522:513:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:that are, e.g., progressive, flat or regressive; they can propose high marginal tax rates
4:98:5743:17:18:90:522:496:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:on the rich or earnings subsidies for the poor, etc. Note that the set of non-linear tax
4:99:5831:18:18:90:522:478:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:policies is a multi-dimensional policy space. With such a policy space, the existence
4:100:5916:18:17:90:522:460:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of a Condorcet winner is not to be expected. This creates a complication for any
4:101:5996:17:18:90:522:443:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:political economy analysis of non-linear tax systems. Our main contribution is to
4:102:6077:18:17:90:522:425:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:provide a characterization of the non-linear income tax system that emerges in a
4:103:6157:17:18:90:522:408:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:political equilibrium with endogenous turnout. Another contribution is to provide
4:104:6238:18:18:90:439:390:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:sufficient conditions for the existence of a pure strategy equilibrium.
4:105:6309:18:17:107:521:372:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Equilibria with endogenous turnout are driven by strategic considerations that
4:106:6387:17:18:90:522:355:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:have no analogue in models with exogenous turnout. With exogenous turnout, parties
4:107:6469:18:18:90:522:337:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:“only” need to check whether they can deviate from a hypothetical equilibrium policy
4:108:6553:18:17:90:522:319:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:to an alternative that makes a larger set of voters better off – of course, taking account
4:109:6643:17:18:90:522:302:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of the incentive and resource constraints that define the set of admissible tax policies.
4:110:6732:18:17:90:522:284:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:With endogenous turnout, a larger set of supporters no longer translates automatically
4:111:6818:17:18:90:522:267:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:into a larger probability of winning. An increase of the set of supporters may lead to
4:112:6904:18:18:90:522:249:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:a decrease in the probability of winning. For instance, if party 1’s proposal becomes
4:113:6989:18:17:90:522:231:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:more similar to the proposal of party 2, this may increase the set of individuals who
4:114:7074:17:18:90:522:214:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:like party 1’s proposal better while at the same time reducing their incentive to vote.
4:115:7161:18:18:90:522:196:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Why bother to vote when the proposals are similar anyway, if the agent has no strong
4:116:7245:18:17:90:298:178:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:idiosyncratic preference for either party?
4:117:7287:17:18:107:521:161:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Our main result is to show that the equilibrium policy has a particularly simple
4:118:7367:18:17:90:522:143:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:form. The equilibrium is symmetric, i.e., both parties propose the same policy in
4:119:7448:17:18:90:522:126:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:equilibrium. The equilibrium policy is determined by a weighted sum of two terms,
4:120:7529:18:18:90:522:108:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:one reflecting a party’s benefit from mobilizing its own supporters and one reflecting
4:121:7615:18:0:90:522:90:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the benefit from demobilizing the supporters of the other party. The weights are gov-
5:122:7701:0:18:90:522:690:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:erned by the distribution of the voters’ party attachments. The intuitive explanation
5:123:7786:18:18:90:522:672:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:is as follows. A party that seeks to win an election has to strike a balance between
5:124:7870:18:17:90:522:654:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:providing benefits to its loyal supporters to get them out to vote and providing bene-
5:125:7956:17:18:90:522:637:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:fits to the most loyal supporters of the rival to make sure that they have no reason to
5:126:8043:18:18:90:522:619:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:vote. Moreover, if a party is unlikely to win, it focuses on its own supporters. If the
5:127:8130:18:17:90:522:601:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:party is the favorite, by contrast, it puts most weight on minimizing turnout in favor
5:128:8216:17:18:90:522:584:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of the opponent. For this reason, a party that is left-leaning in the sense of having
5:129:8301:18:17:90:522:566:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:more loyal supporters with below average income chooses to avoid high taxes on the
5:130:8383:17:18:90:522:549:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:rich whenever it is the likely winner of an election. It chooses to propose significant
5:131:8470:18:18:90:522:531:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:taxes on the rich only if it cannot expect to win. The same logic can explain why
5:132:8551:18:17:90:522:513:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:a party that is supported to a larger extent by voters with above average income
5:133:8631:17:18:90:522:496:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:and expects to win chooses, e.g., not to propose to replace a progressive income tax
5:134:8715:18:18:90:467:478:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:system by a flat tax. It does so only when its chances of winning are low.
5:135:8789:18:17:107:521:460:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Our findings contrast with those of the probabilistic voting models. In these mod-
5:136:8871:17:18:90:522:443:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:els, also known asswing votermodels, participation is exogenous. The parties thus
5:137:8952:18:17:90:522:425:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:do not face a trade-off between maximizing their base and getting their supporters
5:138:9034:17:18:90:522:408:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:out to vote. All parties care about is to maximize their base, as a larger base trans-
5:139:9120:18:18:90:522:390:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:lates mechanically into a larger number of votes. Policy proposals are therefore more
5:140:9205:18:17:90:522:372:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:favorable to voters whose idiosyncratic party preferences are less pronounced. There
5:141:9289:17:18:90:522:355:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:is no point to cater towards citizens who inelastically vote either for party 1 or for
5:142:9375:18:18:90:522:337:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:party 2. With endogenous turnout, by contrast, parties also need to pay attention to
5:143:9459:18:17:90:522:319:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the incentives of their more loyal supporters to come to the ballot. That is, we show
5:144:9544:17:18:90:522:302:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:that the key determinant of policies is not the strength of the response of the swing
5:145:9629:18:17:90:460:284:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:voters but how the party attachments of voters vary with their incomes.
5:146:9700:17:18:107:521:267:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Our findings also contrast with those of the ethical voters models.  With en-
5:147:9777:18:18:90:522:249:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:dogenous payoffs, we find that political equilibrium policies are symmetric, i.e., both
5:148:9864:18:17:90:522:231:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:parties propose the same tax policy. This is not compatible with the assumption in
5:149:9946:17:18:90:522:214:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the literature on endogenous turnout that there is a choice between two well-defined
5:150:10030:18:18:90:522:196:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:and distinct political alternatives. It shows that endogenous turnout does not by itself
5:151:10118:18:17:90:522:178:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:imply that parties have an incentive to differentiate from each other. It is true that
5:152:10204:17:18:90:522:161:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:such differentiation would increase overall turnout. Parties, however, do not seek to
5:153:10289:18:17:90:522:143:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:maximize turnout, but the probability of winning the election. This objective makes
5:154:10372:17:18:90:522:126:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:both parties compromise between mobilizing their own supporters and demobilizing
5:155:10452:18:18:90:522:108:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the other party’s supporters – with the implication that their proposals are identical
5:156:10538:18:0:90:165:90:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:in equilibrium.
6:157:10554:0:18:107:521:690:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Our paper also contributes to the literature on optimal welfare-maximizing tax-
6:158:10633:18:18:90:522:672:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:ation (Mirrlees (1971), Diamond (1998) and Saez (2001)). Specifically, we address
6:159:10714:18:17:90:522:654:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the fundamental question whether welfare-maximizing tax systems have a chance in
6:160:10794:17:18:90:522:637:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the political process, or, put differently, whether the political process gives rise to po-
6:161:10885:18:18:90:522:619:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:litical failures, i.e., to outcomes with undesirable welfare properties. A planner who
6:162:10971:18:17:90:522:601:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:maximizes a concave social welfare function assigns more weight to the well-being
6:163:11052:17:18:90:522:584:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of the poor than to the well-being of the rich.  All else equal, marginal tax rates
6:164:11135:18:17:90:522:566:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:should therefore increase with income. For parties who seek to win an election, the
6:165:11218:17:18:90:522:549:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:well-being of voters has only instrumental value. We derive conditions on primitives –
6:166:11304:18:18:90:522:531:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:i.e., the distribution of party preferences, attitudes towards participation in elections
6:167:11393:18:17:90:522:513:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:and productive abilities – under which parties assign more weight to the well-being
6:168:11476:17:18:90:522:496:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of the rich than to the well-being of the poor, with the consequence that political
6:169:11559:18:18:90:522:478:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:equilibrium tax schedules are incompatible with the maximization of a social welfare
6:170:11643:18:17:90:135:460:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:function.
6:171:11652:17:18:107:521:443:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Our analysis of political failures provides support for the generalized social welfare
6:172:11738:18:17:90:522:425:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:weights of Saez and Stantcheva (2016).  They argue that tax polices are as if a
6:173:11817:17:18:90:522:408:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:generalized social welfare function was maximized that may also reflect non-welfarist
6:174:11902:18:18:90:522:390:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:value judgments or political economy forces. We provide an explicit characterization
6:175:11986:18:17:90:522:372:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of the generalized social welfare weights that correspond to the political equilibrium
6:176:12072:17:18:90:522:355:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:policies in our setup and thereby develop a political economy microfoundation for
6:177:12153:18:18:90:522:337:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:this idea. This provides in particular a rationale for the empirical finding of the high
6:178:12241:18:17:90:485:319:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:implicit social welfare weights on the rich in Lockwood and Weinzierl (2016).
6:179:12318:17:18:107:521:302:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Throughout we make use of functional derivatives for an analysis of political equi-
6:180:12401:18:17:90:522:284:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:librium policies. Piketty (1997) and Saez(2001) introduced the perturbation method
6:181:12483:17:18:90:522:267:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:as an intuitive approach for the characterization of optimal tax systems. A rigorous
6:182:12567:18:18:90:522:249:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:formal analysis of this idea requires the use of functional derivatives, seeGolosov,
6:183:12651:18:17:90:522:231:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Tsyvinski and Werquin(2014). We show that these techniques are also useful for an
6:184:12732:17:18:90:522:214:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:analysis of strategic interaction. First, a game in which two parties maximize the
6:185:12814:18:18:90:522:196:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:probability of winning is a zero sum game. Consequently, a pure strategy equilibrium
6:186:12898:18:17:90:522:178:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:exists if and only if the two parties’ proposals are a saddle point of the function that
6:187:12986:17:18:90:522:161:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:gives party 1’s probability of winning. We use functional derivatives to determine
6:188:13068:18:17:90:522:143:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the conditions under which this function has a saddle point and the existence of pure
6:189:13153:17:18:90:522:126:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:strategy equilibria can be ensured. Second, we use functional derivatives to analyze
6:190:13237:18:18:90:522:108:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:whether the tax policies proposed by different parties are strategic substitutes or com-
6:191:13325:18:0:90:522:90:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:plements. Best response problems – one party choosing a tax policy to maximize its
7:192:13408:0:18:90:522:690:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:probability of winning, taking as given the other party’s proposal – are akin to the
7:193:13492:18:18:90:522:672:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:planning problems studied in the literature on optimal, welfare-maximizing taxation
7:194:13575:18:17:90:522:654:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:only if the best response of one party is independent of the other party’s proposal,
7:195:13659:17:18:90:359:637:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:i.e., only if there is a dominant strategy equilibrium.
7:196:13714:18:18:107:521:619:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The literature on probabilistic voting has focused on the special case of idiosyn-
7:197:13796:18:17:90:522:601:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:cratic party preferences that are drawn from a uniform distribution. With a uniform
7:198:13879:17:18:90:522:584:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:distribution, political equilibrium policies are also the maximizers of a utilitarian so-
7:199:13968:18:17:90:522:566:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:cial welfare function. We show that a uniform distribution, moreover, gives rise to a
7:200:14053:17:18:90:522:549:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:dominant strategy equilibrium, but only under the assumption that turnout is exoge-
7:201:14136:18:18:90:522:531:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:nous. With endogenous turnout, by contrast, the two parties’ best response problems
7:202:14219:18:17:90:522:513:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:are strategically intertwined. An analysis of political competition with endogenous
7:203:14302:17:18:90:522:496:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:turnout is therefore also technically more demanding than the analysis of a proba-
7:204:14384:18:18:90:522:478:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:bilistic voting model with exogenous turnout. We characterize these best responses
7:205:14466:18:34:90:341:460:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:in closed for an arbitrary policy of the opponent.
7:206:14516:34:18:90:521:426:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f5:B:Related literature.Our analysis draws on the literature on the paradox of voting,
7:207:14597:18:17:90:522:408:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:i.e., on the question why people vote even if the chance of affecting the outcome is
7:208:14681:17:18:90:521:391:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:negligible and going to the ballot box somewhat inconvenient.Downs(1957) and
7:209:14757:18:17:90:522:373:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Riker and Ordeshook(1968) are the classical references. Riker and Ordeshook classify
7:210:14841:17:18:90:522:356:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:theories that give rise to the prediction that rational agents do not participate in
7:211:14925:18:18:90:522:338:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:large elections as “positive, but not descriptive.” Various approaches have since been
7:212:15011:18:17:90:522:320:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:explored to come up with a model that explains both participation and abstentions in
7:213:15095:17:18:90:521:303:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:elections, seeFeddersen(2004) for a survey. We draw on one strand of this literature
7:214:15179:18:18:90:522:285:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:due toHarsanyi(1980),Coate and Conlin(2004) andFeddersen and Sandroni(2006).
7:215:15255:18:17:90:522:267:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:In this approach, voters participate in elections because they feel a civic duty to
7:216:15338:17:18:90:522:250:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:vote. More specifically, the civic duty is to follow a participation rule that requires
7:217:15425:18:17:90:522:232:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:an individual to participate if her voting costs are below a cutoff and to abstain
7:218:15507:17:18:90:522:215:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:otherwise. The cutoff is determined by rule-utilitarian calculus that weighs the social
7:219:15594:18:18:90:521:197:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:benefits and the social costs of voting. The framework ofCoate and Conlin(2004) and
7:220:15677:18:17:90:521:179:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Feddersen and Sandroni(2006) not only has plausible comparative statics properties
7:221:15759:17:18:90:522:162:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:but also studies models with a continuum of voters. We are interested in redistributive
7:222:15846:18:18:90:522:144:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:income taxation and employ the workhorse of this literature due toMirrlees(1971).
7:223:15927:18:17:90:522:126:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:The Mirrleesian model also has a continuum of agents. This makes it convenient to
7:224:16008:17:18:90:522:109:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:takeCoate and Conlin(2004) andFeddersen and Sandroni(2006) as the starting
7:225:16082:18:0:90:198:91:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:point of our analysis.
8:226:16105:0:18:107:521:690:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:We use the Mirrleesian model of non-linear income taxation, except that we do not
8:227:16186:18:18:90:522:672:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:impose the assumption that the tax policy is chosen by a benevolent social planner.
8:228:16269:18:17:90:522:654:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:There is a literature that studies political economy forces in connection with non-linear
8:229:16358:17:18:90:522:637:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:taxation. There is, however, no predecessor that relates differences in participation
8:230:16443:18:18:90:522:619:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:in the political process among low, middle and high income classes to the non-linear
8:231:16527:18:17:90:338:601:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:B:tax policies that arise in a political equilibrium.2
8:232:16579:17:18:107:521:584:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:We investigate the welfare properties of political equilibrium policies. We follow
8:233:16661:18:17:90:521:566:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Saez and Stantcheva(2016) who propose to interpret political economy outcomes us-
8:234:16742:17:18:90:522:549:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:ing the notion of generalized social welfare weights. A related approach is taken by
8:235:16826:18:18:90:521:531:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Bierbrauer and Boyer(2016) who provide an analysis of whether analogues to the
8:236:16904:18:17:90:522:513:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:fundamental theorems of welfare economics hold in models of political competition.
8:237:16986:17:18:90:521:496:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Lockwood and Weinzierl(2016) argue that it is difficult to reconcile the social welfare
8:238:17073:18:18:90:522:478:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:weights found empirically with those implied by a social welfare function that values
8:239:17158:18:17:90:522:460:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:redistribution from high to low incomes; taking abstention into account can explain
8:240:17241:17:35:90:155:443:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:B:this finding.3
8:241:17255:35:18:107:521:408:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The remainder is organized as follows. Section1 introduces a general setup for an
8:242:17336:18:18:90:522:390:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:analysis of political competition that connects probabilistic voting with endogenous
8:243:17420:18:17:90:522:372:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:turnout. The implications of this framework for political equilibrium outcomes are
8:244:17502:17:18:90:521:355:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:spelled out in Section2. We characterize political equilibrium tax policies in Section3.
8:245:17590:18:18:89:521:337:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:This section contains the main results of the paper. Section4 clarifies the significance
8:246:17678:18:17:89:521:319:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of endogenous turnout by providing a comparison to a model with exogenous turnout.
8:247:17760:17:18:89:522:302:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:We discuss political failures and equilibrium turnout in Section5. Section6 concludes
8:248:17845:18:17:89:521:284:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:with a discussion of generalized social welfare weights. Unless stated otherwise, proofs
8:249:17933:17:78:89:246:267:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:are relegated to the Appendix.
8:250:17963:78:16:106:522:189:7:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f8:F:2Acemoglu, Golosov and Tsyvinski (2008) and Acemoglu, Golosov and Tsyvinski (2010) embed
8:251:18051:16:12:89:522:173:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:dynamic problems of taxation into the political agency model due toBarro(1973) andFerejohn
8:252:18141:12:12:89:522:161:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:(1986).Farhi et al.(2012) use a probabilistic voting model in which legislatures lack powers of
8:253:18236:12:12:89:522:149:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:commitment to study capital taxation.Bierbrauer and Boyer(2016) study Downsian competition
8:254:18326:12:12:89:521:137:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:when politicians not only propose income tax schedules but also engage in pork-barrel spending.
8:255:18421:12:12:89:522:125:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:Brett and Weymark(2017) andRoell(2012) embed non-linear income taxation into the citizen-

13:404:26515:0:33:90:247:690:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:1 choosesp1so as to maximize

13:406:26589:32:17:90:522:625:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:The characterization of best responses allows us to clarify the logic of the two parties’
13:407:26678:17:18:90:522:608:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:strategic interaction. For instance, it allows us to investigate whether the parties’
13:408:26763:18:18:90:522:590:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:policy proposals are strategic substitutes or complements.  It can also serve as an
13:409:26846:18:17:90:522:572:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:input for an analysis of equilibrium policies. We distinguish between Nash equilibrium
13:410:26932:17:18:90:522:555:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:policies and the policies that arise in a subgame perfect equilibrium.  With both
13:411:27013:18:18:90:522:537:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:solution concepts, the participation probabilities need to constitute an equilibrium of

13:413:27132:32:32:202:409:487:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:A:σ1=σ1∗(p1,p2)andσ2=σ2∗(p1,p2).
13:414:27162:32:32:90:436:455:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:A pair of subgame perfect equilibrium policies(p1,p2)then satisfies
13:415:27229:32:32:90:526:423:12:g_d0_f12:12:g_d0_f11:F: ̄π1(p1,p2)≥ ̄π1( ˆp1,p2),for allˆp1∈Pand ̄π1(p1,p2)≤ ̄π1(p1,ˆp2),for allˆp2∈P .
13:416:27309:32:33:90:401:391:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:A pair of Nash equilibrium policies, by contrast, is such that

13:420:27469:26:18:107:522:283:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:For(p1,p2)to be a Nash equilibrium, it is required that the parties correctly an-
13:421:27550:18:17:90:522:265:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:ticipate turnout and choose polices that maximize their winning probabilities, taking
13:422:27635:17:18:90:522:248:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:this turnout as exogenously given. In a subgame perfect equilibrium, by contrast,
13:423:27716:18:18:90:522:230:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:parties understand that alternative policy choices would also affect the equilibrium
13:424:27800:18:17:90:522:212:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of the participation subgame and take this repercussion into account. We are mainly
13:425:27883:17:18:90:522:195:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:interested in subgame perfect equilibria that are interior, i.e., which are such that
13:426:27968:18:17:90:522:177:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:turnout responds at the margin to changes in proposed policies. The characterization
13:427:28052:17:18:90:522:160:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of Nash equilibria is also of interest, however. First, a non-interior subgame perfect
13:428:28138:18:18:90:522:142:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:equilibrium forces parties to find best replies to turnout rates that are locally unaf-
13:429:28225:18:17:90:522:124:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:fected by changes in the platforms that the parties propose. Nash equilibrium policies
13:430:28311:17:0:90:522:107:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:describe what parties do if turnout does not respond to proposed policies. Second,
14:431:28395:0:18:90:522:690:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:we show that Nash equilibrium policies are also similar to the equilibrium policies in
14:432:28481:18:34:90:469:672:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:a probabilistic voting model with exogenous turnout, a useful benchmark.
14:433:28553:34:18:90:522:638:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f5:B:Remarks on equilibrium existence.The setup introduced so far is very flex-
14:434:28627:18:18:90:522:620:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:ible and nests prominent models of two-party competition.  Models of Downsian
14:435:28704:18:17:90:522:602:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:competition and probabilistic voting models usually impose the assumption that all

14:437:28871:18:18:90:521:567:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:voter typesω, ̃qjv(ω) = 1and hence, ̃qja(ω) =  ̃qju(ω) = 0with probability 1. These
14:438:28954:18:17:90:522:549:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:models differ, however, in their treatment of party preferences. They play no role in

14:449:29207:29:17:90:522:437:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:As is well-known, with a multi-dimensional policy space, pure strategy equilibria typ-
14:450:29293:17:18:90:522:420:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:ically fail to exist in Downsian models of competition. Our analysis below focuses on
14:451:29378:18:18:90:522:402:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:a particular multi-dimensional policy domain, the set of non-linear income tax poli-
14:452:29462:18:17:90:522:384:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:cies. Since our framework nests the Downsian model as a special case, the existence
14:453:29545:17:18:90:373:367:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of pure strategy equilibria cannot be taken for granted.
14:454:29601:18:18:107:521:349:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Appropriate assumptions on the distribution of party preferences ensure existence
14:455:29682:18:17:90:522:331:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:in probabilistic voting models with exogenous turnout. As will become clear below,
14:456:29764:17:18:90:522:314:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Nash equilibria typically exist in our framework under the same conditions as in
14:457:29844:18:17:90:299:296:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:conventional probabilistic voting models.
14:458:29885:17:18:107:521:279:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The models on endogenous participation in large elections assume that for all voter
14:459:29968:18:18:90:522:261:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:typesω, ̃qjv(ω) = 0and hence, ̃qju(ω) +  ̃qja(ω) = 1with probability 1. An implication
14:460:30054:18:17:90:522:243:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:is that a party’s probability of winning is equal to the probability of attracting more
14:461:30141:17:18:90:522:226:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:rule-utilitarian voters than the opponent. Below, we provide conditions on primitives
14:462:30226:18:45:90:468:208:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:that ensure the existence of a subgame-perfect equilibrium in this setting.
14:463:30301:45:29:90:378:163:17:g_d0_f4:17:g_d0_f4:C:2  An equilibrium characterization
14:464:30335:29:18:90:522:134:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:We provide an equilibrium characterization that allows to study specific policies in
14:465:30419:18:17:90:522:116:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the context of our model.  We later use these insights for an analysis of political
14:466:30502:17:0:90:522:99:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:competition over non-linear tax systems. As the first main result, we demonstrate in
15:467:30588:0:18:90:522:690:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:this section that parties face a tradeoff between maximizing their turnout advantage
15:468:30672:18:18:90:222:672:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:and the size of their base.
15:469:30699:18:17:107:521:654:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:From now on, we followCoate and Conlin(2004) andFeddersen and Sandroni

15:471:30852:18:18:90:522:619:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:how high their voting costs are, i.e., every citizen is either of the rule-utilitarian or of
15:472:30944:18:26:90:192:601:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the abstaining type.
15:473:30964:26:26:90:462:575:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f9:C:Assumption 2.For allω, ̃q1v(ω) = 0and ̃q2v(ω) = 0with probability 1.
15:474:31032:26:17:107:522:549:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Harsanyi(1980) also allowed for voters who feel a civic duty to vote but do not

15:476:31195:18:17:89:521:514:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:that includes such voters and gives rise to an equilibrium analysis that is equivalent
15:477:31281:17:26:89:320:497:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:to the one developed in the body of the text.

17:571:36644:18:18:89:521:173:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:turnout (and increases the turnout of the other party) by moving to the left. The
17:572:36725:18:27:89:264:155:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:following Proposition summarizes.

18:578:37052:32:17:107:521:625:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Proposition 1 shows that, with an interior equilibrium of the turnout subgame,

19:616:39203:0:27:90:522:690:17:g_d0_f4:17:g_d0_f4:F:3  Subgame perfect equilibrium and non-linear in-
19:617:39252:27:30:117:232:663:17:g_d0_f4:17:g_d0_f4:C:come taxation
19:618:39265:30:17:90:522:633:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:It is a stylized fact that individuals with high incomes are more likely to participate
19:619:39352:17:18:90:522:616:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:in an election than individuals with low incomes. Studying how the endogeneity of
19:620:39433:18:18:90:522:598:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:turnout affects equilibrium policies therefore is most interesting for polices that affect
19:621:39523:18:17:90:522:580:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the rich and the poor differently. Our main focus is thus on the tax and transfer
19:622:39604:17:18:90:522:563:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:system – as opposed to, say, infrastructure investment or national defense (which we
19:623:39688:18:17:90:522:545:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:cover in AppendixE). Thereby we can also shed light on the following important
19:624:39766:17:18:90:522:528:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:question. Papers that provide calibrations of welfare-maximizing tax systems often
19:625:39848:18:18:90:522:510:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:suggest that top tax rates should be much higher than currently observed in modern
19:626:39930:18:17:90:521:492:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:democracies, see e.g.Diamond(1998),Saez(2001). Having higher taxes, say, on the
19:627:40009:17:18:90:522:475:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:top 10 percent and using the proceeds in a way that benefits the population at large
19:628:40093:18:18:90:522:457:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:should also be politically feasible. A vast majority would benefit from such a reform,
19:629:40179:18:17:90:521:439:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:see e.g.Bierbrauer and Boyer(2017). So why are the observed taxes on the rich lower
19:630:40262:17:18:89:521:422:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:than the theory predicts? We will show that a political economy analysis that takes
19:631:40345:18:38:89:424:404:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the endogeneity of turnout into account can offer an explanation.
19:632:40410:38:26:89:314:366:14:g_d0_f28:14:g_d0_f28:C:3.1  Non-linear income taxation
19:633:40441:26:17:89:521:340:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:From now on we take the policy domain to consist of redistributive tax policies.
19:634:40521:17:18:89:522:323:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Individuals value after-tax income or private goods consumption denoted bycand
19:635:40599:18:18:89:521:305:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:incur a disutility from the productive effort that is needed to generate pre-tax income
19:636:40686:18:17:89:521:287:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f5:B:y.  The preferences of a typeωindividual over(c,y)-pairs are taken to be quasi-
19:637:40765:17:18:89:521:270:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:linear in private goods consumption and represented by a utility functionc−v(y,ω).
19:638:40847:18:17:89:521:252:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f11:B:The functionvmeasures the cost of productive effort and satisfiesv1>0andv11>
19:639:40923:17:18:89:521:235:12:g_d0_f12:12:g_d0_f5:B:0. Moreover, preferences have the Spence-Mirrlees single crossing property so that
19:640:41005:18:18:89:522:217:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:absolute and marginal effort costs are decreasing in the individual’s type,v2<0and
19:641:41087:18:17:89:522:199:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f5:B:v12<0. This property implies that higher types will end up having higher (before
19:642:41167:17:18:89:521:182:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:and after tax) incomes than lower types. Thus, high types are “the rich” and low
19:643:41247:18:18:89:194:164:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:types are “the poor”.
19:644:41268:18:17:107:522:146:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Partyjproposes a functionTj:R+→Rthat assigns a tax payment to any level

19:647:41490:17:0:89:521:94:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:tax revenue. We use a mechanism design approach to obtain a characterization of

21:697:43599:0:26:90:326:690:14:g_d0_f28:14:g_d0_f28:C:3.2  Subgame perfect equilibrium
21:698:43631:26:17:90:522:664:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:We now turn to the tax functions that constitute a subgame perfect equilibrium. By
21:699:43713:17:18:90:522:647:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Proposition 2, subgame perfect equilibrium policies are associated with a saddle point
21:700:43799:18:0:90:242:629:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f14:B:of the functionψ(y1,y2) :=W
21:701:43826:0:12:243:273:637:6:g_d0_f18:8:g_d0_f16:?:1(y1,y2)
21:702:43834:12:14:234:521:625:8:g_d0_f14:12:g_d0_f5:A:W2(y1,y2). In the following we provide a characterization.
21:703:43892:14:17:89:521:611:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:We begin with an analysis of best responses. As will become clear, a best response
21:704:43974:17:18:89:521:594:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of party 1 is a weighted average of the policy that maximizes the welfare gains that
21:705:44058:18:18:89:521:576:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the supporters of party 1 realize if their party wins,W1(y1,y2), and the policy that
21:706:44142:18:17:90:521:558:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:minimizes the gains of the supporters of party 2 if their party wins,W2(y1,y2). As a
21:707:44226:17:18:90:522:541:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:preliminary step, we consider two auxiliary best response problems for party 1: first,
21:708:44312:18:17:90:522:523:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the problem to maximize what is at the stake for the the supporters of party 1; and
21:709:44395:17:35:90:496:506:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:second, the problem to minimize what is at stake for the supporters of party 2.
21:710:44474:35:17:90:522:471:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:F:3.2.1  Mobilizing the supporters of party 1, demobilizing the supporters
21:711:44546:17:26:131:189:454:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:C:of party 2

26:996:56295:27:17:107:521:142:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Consider the implications of this equilibrium characterization for one of the most

27:1000:56636:0:18:90:522:690:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:party with more attachment from the rich chooses to propose moderate tax rates at

27:1003:56889:17:18:90:522:637:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:a more left-leaning party – a party with a comparatively high support from voters

27:1005:57049:18:17:90:522:601:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the likely winner of the election, low taxes on the rich are valuable as they help to
27:1006:57134:17:18:90:522:584:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:discourage the supporters of the other, more right-leaning party. Only a left leaning
27:1007:57219:18:17:90:522:566:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:party with a small probability of winning chooses to propose high taxes on the rich
27:1008:57302:17:18:90:522:549:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:and hence a large amount of lump-sum redistribution to increase the benefits that its
27:1009:57387:18:18:90:522:531:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:own supporters would realize in the unlikely event that it wins the election. The same
27:1010:57473:18:17:90:522:513:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:logic can explain why a more conservative or pro-market party that is supported to
27:1011:57555:17:18:90:522:496:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:a large extent by voters with above average incomes may not propose to abandon a
27:1012:57635:18:18:90:522:478:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:progressive tax system. If the party is the likely winner of the election, its focus is on
27:1013:57725:18:17:90:522:460:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:weakening the support for the competing leftist party. It therefore chooses to propose
27:1014:57811:17:39:90:455:443:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:a platform that is appealing also to voters with below average incomes.
27:1015:57882:39:25:90:312:404:14:g_d0_f28:14:g_d0_f28:C:3.3  Existence of a saddle point
27:1016:57914:25:18:90:522:379:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Subgame perfect equilibria give rise to a non-trivial strategic interdependence of the
27:1017:58000:18:17:90:522:361:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:parties’ proposals. We noted above that the weighting of information rents that is
27:1018:58082:17:18:90:522:344:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:associated with a best response of party 1 depends on the policy proposed by party
27:1019:58164:18:18:90:522:326:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:2. The possibility that the parties choices are strategic substitutes or complements
27:1020:58248:18:17:90:522:308:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:raises the question whether the existence of pure strategy equilibria can be ensured.
27:1021:58333:17:18:90:522:291:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Matching pennies is the prototype zero-sum game with strategic complements and
27:1022:58411:18:18:90:522:273:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:it is well-known that it does not have a pure strategy equilibrium.  The following
27:1023:58493:18:17:90:522:255:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Proposition shows that upon imposing Assumption1 we can also state sufficient
27:1024:58570:17:28:90:406:238:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:conditions for the existence of a subgame perfect equilibrium.
27:1025:58632:28:17:90:521:210:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f9:F:Proposition 3.Suppose that Assumption1 holds and moreover thats1(ω) =12, for
27:1026:58708:17:18:89:521:193:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:F:allω. Also suppose that there is a numberζso thatα(ω)≤ζ, for allω. Then, a pair
27:1027:58787:18:28:90:417:175:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:C:of policies that satisfies (13) is a saddle point of the functionψ.
27:1028:58854:28:17:107:521:147:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Proposition 3 looks at a symmetric case in which each party attracts fifty percent
27:1029:58936:17:18:90:522:130:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of the electorate in the case that both parties make the same proposal. Moreover, it
27:1030:59020:18:17:90:522:112:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:assumes that the distribution of idiosyncratic party preferences has a wide support, as
27:1031:59107:17:0:90:521:95:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:captured by the assumption thatα(ω)is, for allω, sufficiently small. The proof in the
28:1032:59194:0:18:90:522:690:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Appendix is of a stand alone interest as it shows how to use functional derivatives to
28:1033:59280:18:18:90:522:672:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:check second order conditions that ensure equilibrium existence. The distributional
28:1034:59363:18:17:90:522:654:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:assumptions primarily serve to simplify the analysis. They are stronger than needed
28:1035:59446:17:18:90:522:637:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:as there is a range of close enough distributions for which second order conditions are
28:1036:59533:18:45:90:155:619:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:also fulfilled.
28:1037:59548:45:33:90:520:574:17:g_d0_f4:17:g_d0_f4:F:4  Nash equilibrium vs subgame perfect equilibrium
28:1038:59598:33:26:90:301:541:14:g_d0_f28:14:g_d0_f28:C:4.1  Nash equilibrium policies
28:1039:59628:26:17:90:522:515:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:We now compare subgame perfect equilibrium policies to Nash equilibrium policies.
28:1040:59709:17:18:90:522:498:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Nash equilibrium policies do not take the endogeneity of turnout into account. The
28:1041:59791:18:18:90:522:480:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:comparison therefore allows us to highlight how this endogeneity shapes equilibrium
28:1042:59874:18:17:90:522:462:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:policies. The following Proposition provides a characterization of Nash equilibrium
28:1043:59957:17:18:90:522:445:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:policies. A proof would involve only a straightforward adaptation of the arguments
28:1044:60039:18:27:90:345:427:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:in the proof of Lemma3 and is therefore omitted.

30:1114:63746:26:25:90:459:664:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:C:4.2.1  Preliminaries: using tax schedules as the policy domain
30:1115:63808:25:18:90:522:639:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:We briefly sketch an alternative equilibrium characterization in which the policy do-
30:1116:63893:18:17:90:522:621:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:main is taken to be the set of tax schedules – rather than the set of non-decreasing
30:1117:63977:17:18:90:522:604:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:earnings functions.  This makes it possible to relate our analysis more directly to
30:1118:64060:18:18:90:522:586:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:standard concepts in public finance such as, e.g., the marginal cost of public funds.
30:1119:64145:18:17:90:522:568:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:More importantly, this turns out to be particularly useful for the analysis of whether
30:1120:64231:17:18:90:425:551:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the two parties’ policies are strategic substitutes or complements.
30:1121:64298:18:18:107:521:533:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:As we explained in Section 3.1, we can directly let parties choose nonlinear

30:1124:64529:18:17:90:522:480:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:enue (or loss) generated by the tax reform that we are considering, taking into
30:1125:64608:17:18:90:522:463:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:account the behavioral responses it induces on labor supply, is rebated (or taxed
30:1126:64689:18:18:90:522:445:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:away) lump-sum and uniformly to the population. We can replace the arguments
30:1127:64765:18:17:90:522:427:12:g_d0_f12:12:g_d0_f5:B:(y1,y2)andωof all the functions we consider with(T1,T2)andy1≡y1(ω), re-
30:1128:64836:17:18:89:521:410:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:spectively.  Consider for instance the problem of choosingT1so as to maximize

30:1130:64987:18:17:89:521:374:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:incomesy1that are realized if party 1 is elected. The details of the argument and
30:1131:65068:17:18:89:275:357:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the derivations are in the Appendix.
30:1132:65104:18:17:107:521:339:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Consider a reform of the platformT1in the directionh1along with a lump-sum
30:1133:65178:17:18:89:522:322:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f12:B:rebateR1, so that the tax function proposed by party1becomesy7→T1(y) +

31:1178:66731:34:25:89:379:441:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:C:4.2.2  Analyzing the strategic complementarities
31:1179:66779:25:18:89:521:416:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Subgame perfect and Nash equilibria differ also in the way in which the best response
31:1180:66864:18:18:89:521:398:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of party 1 depends on the proposal of party 2 and vice versa. For a systematic analysis

31:1182:67039:17:18:89:522:363:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:1 proposes a tax schedule analogous to (17), where the weightsG1Win this formula
31:1183:67119:18:18:89:522:345:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:are replaced byGNif its best response seeks to maximize ̄Γ1uand byGSPif it seeks

31:1185:67275:17:18:89:260:310:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:would have to be altered forGSP.

31:1187:67381:17:18:90:522:275:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:policies of different parties are strategic substitutes or complements. For instance, if
31:1188:67469:18:18:90:522:257:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:party 2 moves towards a tax schedule that has higher tax rates at the top, does this
31:1189:67553:18:17:90:522:239:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:imply that party 1’s best response also changes in the direction of higher tax rates
31:1190:67637:17:18:90:522:222:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:at the top?  Functional derivatives can be used to operationalize questions of this
31:1191:67720:18:18:90:522:204:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:type. If the Gateaux differential ofGN(ω|y1,y2)with respect to a change ofy2into
31:1192:67800:18:17:90:522:186:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:a direction of higher marginal tax rates at the top is positive, this implies that party
31:1193:67888:17:18:90:521:169:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:1’s best response will involve lower marginal tax rates on individuals of typeω. If it
31:1194:67974:18:17:90:321:151:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:is negative, it involves higher marginal taxes.

34:1311:73539:17:18:90:521:496:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:with incomey1, so that the best response of party 1 is to decrease the progressivity
34:1312:73623:18:45:90:186:478:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of its tax schedule.
34:1313:73643:45:33:90:325:433:17:g_d0_f4:17:g_d0_f4:C:5  Additional considerations
34:1314:73671:33:26:90:238:400:14:g_d0_f28:14:g_d0_f28:C:5.1  Political failures
34:1315:73694:26:17:90:522:374:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:We now discuss to what extent political equilibrium policies are appealing from a
34:1316:73775:17:18:90:522:357:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:normative perspective. We therefore relate them to the tax policy that maximizes a
34:1317:73857:18:18:90:521:339:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:social welfare functionSWF=E[G(u(ω))], whereGis a concave transformation and
34:1318:73933:18:17:90:521:321:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f5:B:u(ω)is the utility level that a typeωindividual realizes under a given tax policy. Let
34:1319:74019:17:18:90:522:304:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f5:B:gdenote the derivative ofG. Then ̄g(ω|y) :=E[g(u(ω′)|ω′≥ω]is the welfare gain
34:1320:74096:18:17:90:521:286:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:that is realized if all individuals with incomes abovey(ω)are made slightly better off,
34:1321:74183:17:18:90:521:269:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:and the ratioGD(ω|y) := ̄g(ω|y) ̄g(ω|y)relates this welfare gain to the one that would be
34:1322:74272:18:18:90:522:251:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:obtained under a tax reform that raises everybody’s utility – i.e., the denominator is
34:1323:74358:18:27:90:269:233:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the marginal value of public funds.
34:1324:74393:27:18:90:521:206:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f9:F:Proposition 6. (Diamond, 1998)A welfare maximizing tax system is such that,
34:1325:74468:18:27:90:137:188:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:C:for allω,
34:1326:74477:27:16:156:200:161:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f12:C:T′(y(ω))
34:1327:74485:16:0:146:210:145:12:g_d0_f12:12:g_d0_f12:C:1−T′(y(ω))
34:1328:74495:0:0:226:260:153:12:g_d0_f12:12:g_d0_f13:C:=−

34:1331:74507:0:0:312:389:153:12:g_d0_f12:12:g_d0_f12:A:(1−GD(ω|y))
34:1332:74518:0:16:394:458:161:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f12:C:v21(y(ω),ω))
34:1333:74530:16:0:398:454:145:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f12:C:v1(y(ω),ω)
34:1334:74540:0:35:463:522:153:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f5:A:.(22)
34:1335:74545:35:18:107:522:118:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:We omit a formal proof of Proposition6 as it requires only a straightforward
34:1336:74621:18:0:90:521:100:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:adaptation of the proof of Lemma3.  With a concave social welfare function, the
35:1337:74702:0:18:90:521:690:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:weighting functionGD(· |y)is decreasing. Ceteris paribus, i.e. keeping the inverse
35:1338:74784:18:18:90:522:672:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:hazard rate and the elasticity of labor supply constant – marginal tax rates should
35:1339:74867:18:17:90:249:654:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:therefore increase with income.
35:1340:74898:17:18:107:521:637:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:This observation is useful for a welfare analysis of political equilibrium outcomes.
35:1341:74982:18:18:90:521:619:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:If a weighting function for information rentsGcan be derived from a social welfare
35:1342:75064:18:17:89:521:601:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:function, thenω′< ωimplies thatG(ω′|y)≥ G(ω|y)as individuals with lower
35:1343:75135:17:18:89:521:584:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:income cannot receive a lower weight in the social welfare function. If the weighting
35:1344:75220:18:17:89:521:566:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:function associated with a political equilibrium violates this monotonicity property
35:1345:75304:17:18:89:521:549:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:then we can conclude that the political outcome is incompatible with the objective
35:1346:75386:18:18:89:443:531:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f9:B:of welfare-maximization. We then say that there is apolitical failure.
35:1347:75456:18:17:107:521:513:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Depending on the primitives, both Nash and subgame perfect equilibria may give
35:1348:75534:17:18:89:521:496:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:rise to such political failures. For instance, with a uniform distribution of idiosyncratic
35:1349:75625:18:18:89:522:478:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:party preferences (Assumption1),GN(ω|y1,y2)is given by expression (15), so that
35:1350:75704:18:17:90:522:460:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:ifαis constant across types but the inclination to vote increases with income, so that
35:1351:75790:17:18:90:522:443:12:g_d0_f12:12:g_d0_f5:B: ̄quis an increasing function, then Nash equilibrium policies give rise to a political
35:1352:75876:18:17:90:522:425:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:failure. Now consider subgame perfect equilibrium policies, again under Assumption
35:1353:75958:17:18:90:521:408:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:1. Recall thatGsSP(ω)is a convex combination of two weighting functionsG1WandG2W,
35:1354:76039:18:18:90:521:390:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:where the weight onG1Wis low if party 1 has a high chance of winning. Suppose that
35:1355:76121:18:17:90:521:372:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f5:B:s1is a decreasing function ands2an increasing function, then the weighting function
35:1356:76204:17:18:90:522:355:12:g_d0_f13:12:g_d0_f5:B:G1Wis decreasing and the weighting functionG2Wis increasing. In this scenario, if
35:1357:76285:18:18:90:522:337:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:party 1’s winning probability is sufficiently close to one, subgame perfect equilibrium
35:1358:76372:18:37:90:279:319:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:policy gives rise to a political failure.
35:1359:76413:37:26:90:266:282:14:g_d0_f28:14:g_d0_f28:C:5.2  Equilibrium turnout
35:1360:76437:26:17:90:522:256:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Parties in our model do not care about turnout by itself. They care about turnout
35:1361:76518:17:18:90:522:239:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:only to the extent that it increases their probability of winning an election.  For

35:1363:76686:17:18:90:522:204:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:parties prefer a large share in small set of voters over a small share in a large set of

36:1409:78577:18:18:107:521:298:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Previous analyses of ethical voter models by Coate and Conlin (2004) and Fed-

36:1418:79314:18:17:107:521:139:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Our analysis has no straightforward analogue to the finding that polarization

37:1425:79885:18:18:90:521:619:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:on how turnout varies with ̄W. In our setting the expected benefits of the supporters
37:1426:79970:18:17:90:522:601:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of parties 1 and 2 do not add up to a constant, so that we cannot perform a similar
37:1427:80053:17:18:90:522:584:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:exercise. The observations that equilibria are symmetric and that a deviation from
37:1428:80135:18:17:90:522:566:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:equilibrium policies would increase overall turnout is therefore a related finding. It
37:1429:80221:17:45:90:496:549:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:shows that a lack of polarization leaves room for an increase of overall turnout.
37:1430:80302:45:30:90:494:504:17:g_d0_f4:17:g_d0_f4:C:6  Conclusion: endogenous social welfare weights
37:1431:80350:30:17:90:522:474:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:The theory of optimal taxation characterizes the tax policy that would be chosen by
37:1432:80433:17:18:90:522:457:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:a benevolent social planner with the objective to maximize social welfare. However,
37:1433:80516:18:18:90:522:439:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:there are many “reasonable” social welfare functions. The literature then often refers
37:1434:80602:18:17:90:522:421:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:to “society’s social welfare function” as the relevant one but typically does not provide
37:1435:80691:17:18:90:522:404:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:a precise formulation of how society would come to agree on a given social welfare
37:1436:80773:18:17:90:522:386:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:function. Still there are attempts to identify society’s social welfare function empiri-
37:1437:80861:17:18:90:522:369:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:cally. The idea is to use theABCformula for welfare-maximizing taxation (22), data
37:1438:80943:18:18:90:522:351:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:on the tax system, the earnings distribution and labor supply elasticities to map out
37:1439:81028:18:17:90:522:333:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:society’s social welfare weightsG, see e.g. Blundell et al. (2009).Bargain et al.(2011),
37:1440:81116:17:18:89:460:316:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Zoutman, Jacobs and Jongen(2016) orLockwood and Weinzierl(2016).
37:1441:81180:18:18:107:522:298:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Propositions4 and   6 and Theorem1 contain differentABC-formulas. Proposition
37:1442:81257:18:17:89:521:280:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:4 gives the tax rates that are predicted by a swing voter model with exogenous
37:1443:81335:17:18:89:522:263:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:turnout, Proposition6 characterizes welfare-maximizing taxes, and Theorem1 takes
37:1444:81415:18:17:89:521:245:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:into account the endogeneity of turnout. Each of these formulas provides a different
37:1445:81499:17:18:89:522:228:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:interpretation of theG-term that can be mapped out given data on the tax system, the
37:1446:81583:18:18:89:521:210:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:earnings distribution and labor supply elasticities. The data cannot tell us, however,
37:1447:81669:18:17:89:521:192:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:how plausible these different interpretations are. This requires criteria external to
37:1448:81754:17:18:89:521:175:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the formal framework developed here. What we can say, however, is that it makes
37:1449:81833:18:18:89:521:157:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:little sense to let the data speak about what society’s social welfare function looks
37:1450:81918:18:17:89:521:139:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:like without at the same time having an explanation for how society would come to
37:1451:81999:17:18:89:304:122:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:settle on a specific social welfare function.
37:1452:82044:18:0:107:521:104:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:In fact, Arrow’s impossibility shows that it may be entirely infeasible to aggregate
38:1453:82130:0:18:90:522:690:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:individual preferences over tax policies into a social welfare function. What is feasible,
38:1454:82220:18:18:90:522:672:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:by contrast, is to reinterpret any process that selects a tax schedule from the set of
38:1455:82306:18:17:90:522:654:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Pareto-efficent tax schedules as if it was the choice of an agent with preferences over
38:1456:82393:17:18:90:521:637:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the set of Pareto-optima, see Samuelson(1967).Saez and Stantcheva(2016) recognize
38:1457:82474:18:18:90:522:619:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:that observed tax policies are not entirely driven by welfare considerations, but also by
38:1458:82563:18:17:90:522:601:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:non-welfarist value judgments or political economy forces. They propose to capture
38:1459:82645:17:18:90:522:584:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:these forces by means of generalized social welfare functions.  Thus, observed tax
38:1460:82727:18:17:90:522:566:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:policies are interpreted as if there had been an agent who made a selection from
38:1461:82807:17:18:90:522:549:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the set of Pareto optima and who used a generalized social welfare function for this
38:1462:82891:18:18:90:133:531:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:purpose.
38:1463:82899:18:17:107:521:513:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:In the preceding analysis we have analyzed a strategic game between political par-
38:1464:82981:17:18:90:522:496:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:ties who propose non-linear tax schedules to an electorate that consists of individuals
38:1465:83068:18:18:90:522:478:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:with heterogenous incomes. We have shown that political equilibrium tax policies can
38:1466:83152:18:17:90:522:460:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:be represented byABC-formulas akin to those that are used to characterize welfare-
38:1467:83234:17:18:90:522:443:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:maximizing tax systems. Thus our analysis provides a detailed and microfounded
38:1468:83312:18:17:90:522:425:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:formalization that political economy forces can indeed be captured by generalized
38:1469:83393:17:18:90:522:408:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:social welfare weights. Moreover, we emphasize that these generalized social welfare
38:1470:83477:18:18:90:522:390:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:weights are objects which are endogenous to the political process and, in particular,
38:1471:83562:18:17:90:522:372:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:that alternative models of political competition give rise to alternative social welfare
38:1472:83650:17:18:90:522:355:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:weights. We have also shown that political equilibrium outcomes may be incompat-
38:1473:83730:18:18:90:522:337:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:ible with the maximization of a concave social welfare function. Generalized social
38:1474:83813:18:17:90:522:319:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:welfare weights are therefore needed. The class of traditional social welfare weights
38:1475:83898:17:45:90:282:302:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:cannot capture such political failures.

51:2139:101458:39:22:90:522:624:14:g_d0_f28:14:g_d0_f28:F:Variational approach: using tax schedules as the policy domain
51:2140:101520:22:15:90:522:602:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:We briefly sketch an alternative equilibrium characterization in which the policy domain is taken to
51:2141:101620:15:14:90:522:587:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:be the set of tax schedules – rather than the set of non-decreasing earnings functions. This makes
51:2142:101718:14:15:90:522:573:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:it possible to relate our analysis more directly to standard concepts in public finance such as, e.g.,
51:2143:101820:15:14:90:522:558:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:the marginal cost of public funds. More importantly, this turns out to be particularly useful for the
51:2144:101921:14:15:90:462:544:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:analysis of whether the two parties’ policies are strategic substitutes or complements.
51:2145:102008:15:15:107:522:529:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:As we explained in Section3.1, we can directly let parties choose nonlinear tax schedules, i.e.,
51:2146:102104:15:14:90:522:514:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:twice continuously differentiable functionsTj:R+→R. To prevent parties from arbitrarily raising
51:2147:102199:14:15:90:522:500:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:agents’ utilities by lowering their taxes, we must impose that any tax reform that a party can propose
51:2148:102301:15:14:90:522:485:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:is budget-neutral. Without loss of generality, this is equivalent to imposing that any extra revenue
51:2149:102401:14:15:90:522:471:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:(or loss) generated by the tax reform that we are considering, taking into account the behavioral
51:2150:102498:15:15:90:522:456:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:responses it induces on labor supply, is rebated (or taxed away) lump-sum and uniformly to the
51:2151:102592:15:14:90:522:441:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:population. Since there is a one-to-one map between earnings functions and tax schedules, we can
51:2152:102688:14:0:90:186:427:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:replace the arguments
51:2153:102709:0:8:188:193:435:10:g_d0_f17:10:g_d0_f17:?:(
51:2154:102710:8:0:193:216:427:10:g_d0_f22:7:g_d0_f24:?:y1,y2
51:2155:102715:0:8:217:222:435:10:g_d0_f17:10:g_d0_f17:?:)
51:2156:102716:8:0:225:382:427:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:?:of all the functions we consider with
51:2157:102753:0:8:385:390:435:10:g_d0_f17:10:g_d0_f17:?:(
51:2158:102754:8:0:389:417:427:10:g_d0_f22:7:g_d0_f24:?:T1,T2
51:2159:102759:0:8:417:422:435:10:g_d0_f17:10:g_d0_f17:?:)
51:2160:102760:8:15:422:522:427:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:. Moreover, since there
51:2161:102783:15:14:90:522:412:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:is a one-to-one map between types and incomes for a given tax schedule, we can use interchangeably
51:2162:102881:14:15:90:328:398:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:the argumentsωory1≡y1(ω)for all of our variables.
51:2163:102930:15:26:107:489:383:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:A:Consider for instance the problem of choosingT1so as to maximizeW1(T1,T2), where

61:3279:120792:45:26:89:224:274:17:g_d0_f4:17:g_d0_f4:C:E  Public goods
61:3280:120807:26:15:89:521:248:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:Our framework for studying endogenous turnout and endogenous platforms in political competition
61:3281:120902:15:14:89:521:233:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:is developed for a generic policy domain. We have emphasized that the set of non-linear income tax
61:3282:121000:14:15:89:521:219:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:systems is a policy domain of particular interest. That said, our framework can also be applied to
61:3283:121098:15:15:89:521:204:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:study the implications of endogenous turnout for political competition over other policy domains.
61:3284:121195:15:14:89:521:189:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:In this section, we briefly summarize the results from such an analysis. Specifically, we report on
61:3285:121294:14:15:89:356:175:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:the implications of our framework for public goods provision.
61:3286:121355:15:14:107:522:160:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:Individuals have preferences over public goods that are given byu(ω,p) =ω p−k(p), where
61:3287:121442:14:15:89:522:146:10:g_d0_f22:10:g_d0_f8:F:p∈R+denotes the quantity of the public good,ω∈Ωis an individual’s public goods preference
61:3288:121531:15:26:89:522:131:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:and the cost functionkcaptures the per capita cost of public goods provision.14We begin with a
61:3289:121625:26:15:102:522:105:7:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f8:F:14In an economy with a continuum of individuals and private information on public goods prefer-

62:3291:121824:0:15:90:522:690:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:characterization of the public good provision level that party 1 would choose if its sole objective was
62:3292:121927:15:27:90:483:675:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:to mobilize its supporters. In this case, it would chooseq1with the objective to maximize
62:3293:122016:27:27:198:414:648:10:g_d0_f22:10:g_d0_f22:?:W1(p1,p2) =E[G1W(ω p1−k(p1)−u(p2,ω)|ω)].
62:3294:122056:27:29:90:420:621:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:Givenp2, the first order condition characterizing the optimal choice ofp1is
62:3295:122131:29:0:115:122:592:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:?:E

62:3303:122221:30:15:89:521:562:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:This first order condition is a political economy analogue to the Samuelson rule for first-best public
62:3304:122323:15:14:89:521:547:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:good provision. For the given setup, the Samuelson rule stipulates thatE[ω] =k′(p), i.e., it requires
62:3305:122424:14:15:90:522:533:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:equal weights for all public goods preferences. For the purpose of mobilizing its supporters, party
62:3306:122523:15:15:90:522:518:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:1 does not apply equal weights.  Instead the public good preferences of different individuals are

62:3314:122815:27:0:90:235:435:10:g_d0_f8:7:g_d0_f23:F:and the policy that maximizesW

62:3317:122870:23:27:242:366:409:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f25:?:E[GSP(ω|p1,p2)ω] =k′(p1)
62:3318:122894:27:15:89:114:382:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:where

62:3320:122964:25:17:90:522:342:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:Again, the party compromises between mobilizing its own supporters and demobilizing the support-
62:3321:123060:17:18:90:522:325:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:ers of the other party – with the weight on the own supporters being smaller if the party is more
62:3322:123157:18:34:90:147:307:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:likely to win.
62:3323:123171:34:18:90:522:273:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:F:Strategic substitutes and complements: Public goods vs non-linear taxa-
62:3324:123242:18:22:90:113:255:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:C:tion
62:3325:123246:22:15:90:522:233:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:For public good provision, it is particularly easy to determine whether the provision levels of different
62:3326:123351:15:22:90:323:218:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:parties are substitutes or complements. Suppose that
62:3327:123403:22:13:248:253:196:10:g_d0_f22:10:g_d0_f22:?:∂
62:3328:123404:13:0:243:258:183:10:g_d0_f22:7:g_d0_f24:?:∂p2
62:3329:123407:0:29:260:369:190:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f22:?:E[GSP(ω|p1,p2)ω]>0,
62:3330:123426:29:15:90:521:161:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:i.e., that an increase of party 2’s provision level leads to an increase of theGSP-weighted average of
62:3331:123528:15:56:90:522:146:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:public goods preferences. Then the best response of party 1 is to also increase its provision level,
62:3332:123628:56:0:90:311:90:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:and anonymity, see Bierbrauer and Hellwig(2016).
63:3333:123678:0:22:90:400:690:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:i.e., the parties choices are then strategic complements. If, by contrast,
63:3334:123752:22:14:248:253:668:10:g_d0_f22:10:g_d0_f22:?:∂
63:3335:123753:14:0:243:258:654:10:g_d0_f22:7:g_d0_f24:?:∂p2
63:3336:123756:0:29:260:369:661:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f22:?:E[GSP(ω|p1,p2)ω]<0,
63:3337:123775:29:15:90:219:632:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:they are strategic substitutes.
63:3338:123806:15:14:107:521:617:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:For non-linear income taxation, this analysis is more complicated as it has to be applied sep-
63:3339:123900:14:15:90:522:603:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:arately for each level of income. There may be a complementarity in marginal tax rates for high
63:3340:123995:15:14:90:522:588:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:incomes and a substitutability in marginal tax rates for low incomes, etc. A public good is jointly
63:3341:124094:14:15:90:522:574:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:consumed by all individuals. One cannot have a high public good provision level for some people
63:3342:124189:15:14:90:522:559:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:and a low public good provision level for others. This simplifies the analysis of the parties’ strategic
63:3343:124293:14:15:90:163:545:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:interdependence.
63:3344:124309:15:15:107:521:530:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:For non-linear income taxation, the formal expression that allows us to analyze how strategic
63:3345:124402:15:14:90:522:515:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:substitutabilities and complementarities vary with incomes or productive abilities is the Gateaux
63:3346:124499:14:15:90:521:501:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:differential of the weighting functionsG. This Gateaux differential is a function, it gives a different
63:3347:124602:15:14:90:521:486:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:value for each typeω. For public good provision, we only have to look at how a population average
63:3348:124699:14:15:90:522:472:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:of public goods preferences changes with the parties proposals. The formal analysis therefore does
63:3349:124797:15:0:90:356:457:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:F:not require functional derivatives but only standard calculus.
